text:
This is sooo good! I, too, only added 1/2 c sugar. I never use half and half so I decided to use evaporated milk instead. I didn't want to waste the other 8 oz of evap milk so I just poured the 12 oz can into a 4 c measure and then filled with milk and heated it all. I didn't bother with adding some cold milk to the hot chocolate. Yum Yum, just what I wanted on a cool morning, thanks Jeanie Bean!

text:
OMG - this is the best cocoa!!!  I made it as the recipe stated and it was overly sweet for my taste.  Then made it per the reviewers suggestions and it was much, much better!  Definitely decrease the sugar to 1/2 cup; your blood sugar levels will thank you!!!  Increased the vanilla to 1 teaspoon and a note of caution - DO NOT use cheap vanilla as you can taste the difference between good vanilla and the inexpensive type sold in the supermarket.  You'll be glad you did...  Thanks Jeanie for submitting this great recipe!  Definitely a keeper!!!

text:
I am sipping this cocoa as I type this review.  It is very very good!  Much better than any crud you get in the packets, you know that there aren't any dyes or anything artificial in this which is why I choose to hand-make our cocoa.  

I gave it a 5 star rating but it is  very, very sweet! And I have a sweet tooth!  ***AND*** I only used 1/2 C sugar.  I would definitey not use the 3/4 C, it will be too sickening sweet. 

To make it less sweet you could either decrease the sugar amount further or add more hot water, I suppose.

Overall great alternative to the store bought "stuff".

text:
Move over Swiss Miss! With each sip, I'm liking this hot cocoa recipe more and more. It is incredibly rich and creamy, and the taste is absolutely out of this world. The recipe is fairly simple, but a few tips can make it even simpler. To judge when the hot cocoa is ready to be removed from the heat, place your hand over the steam coming from the pot. If you cannont keep it there without feeling significant heat after 4 seconds, the cocoa is ready! If you do not want to divide the cocoa into four mugs, add the entire 1/2 cup of cream into the pot along with the vanilla, and portion as you please. Reduce the amount of sugar to 1/2 cup if you are looking for a bolder, more bitter flavor, but adding all 3/4 cup seems to make it just sweet enough. This recipe is absolutely perfect for the cold winter day! Three cheers for Jeanie!

text:
Easy to make for one! Need a 2c. mug, small whisk, 1T. and 1/8 tsp. measure, & microwave. Place 2T. water, 2 1/2 T. cocoa, 1T. sugar, and pinch of salt in bottom of mug. Stir with small whisk. Microwave 1 minute. Whisk in 1 1/2c. milk and microwave 2 1/2 minutes. For full-bodied taste stir in 1/8 t. vanilla, 1/8 t. almond extract, & 1T. half & half or whipping cream. Sprinkle top with cinnamon and stir. This gives you a tasty way to get 50% of your daily calcium and leaves hardly any dishes to wash!

text:
WAY too sweet. 1/2 cup of sugar is just about right for most tastes (we like it with even about one Tb less than that.) A tiny pinch (whatever you can hold between your index finger and thumb only) of baking soda helps smooth out the acidity of the cocoa, if you're not using a Dutch process brand like Droste. The standard Hershey cocoa will benefit from that tiny addition.

text:
ABSOLUTELY DELICIOUS!  I am sipping it, while I type this review!  This has a wonderful, creamy flavor.  I did REDUCE THE SUGAR and per other reviewers advice, used half a cup of sugar.  Other that that, I followed the directions exactly as written, and did not change anything else.

One thing I would recommend is DO NOT ADD THE CREAM TO THE BOTTOM OF THE MUG.  When I poured the hot chocolate into the mug with the cream, it was not even lukewarm! That was due to the cream, being in the mug already!  Add the cream AFTER you pour your hot chocolate, not before.  

Also (and this is just my personal preference), I did use all organic ingredients.

In the directions where you add milk and then heat UNTIL HOT, I would HIGLY RECOMMEND at this point, BRINGING IT TO A GENTLE BOIL and immediately remove from heat. THEN, pour in your cream.   

FIVE STARS!  Love this!  Jeanie Bean, thank you so much for sharing this recipe!  It's a keeper.

text:
When temperatures drop from 80 to 25 overnight, you need a great hot cocoa recipe! I made the cocoa for some guests, and they loved it! If you use marshmallow's, 1/2 cup sugar is perfect, but if not, 3/4 cup of sugar works best. I did add 1/4 cup milk chocolate chips. I will definitely use this recipe again! **Made this again...to celebrate the putting up of our christmas tree:) I was out of milk, so I used a mixture of 1/2 & 1/2 and evaporated milk. I had some homemade caramel, so I added just a bit to the cocoa. We had toppings of marshmallows, crushed original andes mints and crushed candy cane andes mints. Again, this was a hit!

text:
Not bad.... While I enjoyed this, I prefer Verushka's candy cane cocoa just a smidgin more (I LOOOVE anything minty). What I did like aobut this was the addition of half-and-half cream. I like my cocoa lukewarm. Adding chilled half-half cooled it down to a perfect drinkable temperature! My only issue with this is how sweet it was (but that's an easy fix). I will definitely make this again, but will be SURE to decrease the amount of sugar (or use all sugar substitute or a combination of sugar / substitute instead). NOTE: This recipe will give you 4 VERY small cups of cocoa. If you use large mugs like I do, you'll find that this yields more like 2 servings worth. I halved this (just making a cup for myself) and it filled my large mug with about 1/4 c. leftover. Topped with whipped cream and chocolate sprinkles. Thanks for sharing, Jeanie Bean! This was a great way to warm up on this chilly Midwest afternoon! :-)

text:
I tried out this recipe just last night and I loved it! I followed the suggestions and lowered the amount of sugar from 3/4 cup to 1/2 cup, and I was glad I did. The sweetness was just right with only 1/2 cup. I also tweaked the recipe a bit more. I lowered the amount of milk to 3 cups and added in the 1/2 cup half and half while the the hot cocoa was still in the saucepan. I also added the vanilla in while it was still in the saucepan. And also, what I found is that once I was done combining everything that it wasn't hot enough for my liking. So I just let it warm up for a bit while stirring occasionally and it turned out perfect! Also tastes wonderful with a bit of whipped cream added on top.

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/1471239.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Excellent in small batches--settles when made in large batches.  We prepared a quadruple batch for our daughter's January birthday party.  It was very rich and chocolaty!  Those who love sweet drinks will be pleased.  Those who prefer things a bit less sugary will likely prefer a version with reduced sugar.  By the time the drink cools from hot to lukewarm, though, a lot of the sugar and chocolate have settled to the bottom of the cup, making those last few sips SO sweet and rich that it's almost hard to swallow.  If you can drink it hot or don't mind stirring as you sip, this is a delicious recipe.  For those without a sweet tooth or those looking for something to make in large batches and serve over the course of a party (during which the stuff is settling in the pot), I'd suggest trying another recipe or reducing the sugar.

text:
During our last midwest snow storm, my husband turned to me and said "hot chocolate would be so good right now!"  I agreed with him immediately, but knew I didn't have any packets or chocolate syrup.  However, I just knew that my trusty ol' allrecipes.com wouldn't let me down!  This recipe was a cinch to throw together and is so good that I have been informed I'm no longer allowed to make hot chocolate any other way.  On the second batch, we had quite a bit left over and I was curious to see what would happen when it was refrigerated.  So I poured it into a lidded mason jar and stashed it.  The next day, it made incredibly delicious chocolate milk.  The flavor is quite concentrated, so we cut it about 50/50 with milk.  Very, very good!  I haven't tried yet, but I'm sure it could be reheated in a mug in the microwave to enjoy a second round of hot chocolate.  Wonderful recipe Jeanie!

I combine the cocoa, sugar and salt, store it in an air tight container and use it as ready serve cocoa drink powder. I warm 1 cup of milk add a heaping dessert spoon of the cocoa mix for my kids every morning. If you are using cold milk, pour a teeny bit of milk into the bottom of the glass, add the powder and stir until it makes a syrup, then add the rest of your milk or else the cocoa powder won't mix in.

This is very similar to the Hershey's cocoa recipe, but then again it takes the same few ingredients to make a basic hot chocolate. This is a really good recipe though you do have to bit of work to get it perfect. The first time I tried it I followed the recipe exactly and I used Hersheyâs cocoa powder and the chocolate flavor was "ok". The next time I used high quality (French) Valrhona Cocoa Powder and 1/3 cup was way too strong. Today I made it with half the normal amount of Valrhona cocoa powder (1/6 cup) and it was wonderfully celestial. With 1/6 cup Valrhona the flavor was well balanced with the other ingredients yet it was a lot more complex than just using 1/3 cup of the Hersheys.  Another area I had to make some changes was the amount of sugar; waaayyy to sweet with Â¾ cup white sugar. Instead I used Â½ cup of freshly ground raw Mexican sugar (piloncillo) and it was perfect (and the raw sugar gives a nice âhint of caramelâ taste). Also to add a slight twist I used Â¼ teaspoon of fresh ground real cinnamon.  With these changes the recipe turned from a good hot cocoa recipe to an outstandingly complex yet balanced and not too rich cocoa, Iâd be willing to pay good money for. Too bad Starbucks doesnât sell this kind of quality hot cocoa.  Variants; 1/6 cup Valrhona Cocoa powder  	Â½ cup raw (piloncillo) sugar  	optional = Â¼ tsp fresh cinnamon  	everything else the same

country:
None
text:
Yum!  Here's how to do it easily in the microwave: In a 4 cup Pyrex measuring cup, put your cocoa (I used a rounded 1/3 c), sugar (I used a rounded 1/3 c), salt, and cold water. Mix with spoon. (It will be quite lumpy).  Microwave  for about 2 minutes, stopping to stir several times.   Microwave more if needed, but keep stirring several times until this syrup is fairly lump-free. Add the vanilla and the milk.  Continue microwaving and stirring a bit until this is hot and creamy (about 5 minutes.)  Pour into mugs and top with 1/ & 1/2 as directed or use whipped cream.  Sooo yummy!!!

text:
My family didn't "love" this recipe, but I made some changes based on other reviews and what I had on hand. I lowered the sugar to half a cup and it was still very sweet. I used almond milk in place of the regular milk and evaporated milk in lieu of the heavy cream because they are what I had on hand. I also added about a cup of strong black coffee (this was only made for adults) to help cut the sweetness.  Overall it's a great basic recipe that is easy to make and customize for particular tastes, etc. I'll definitely make this again during the holiday season. I'll be adding cinnamon and peppermint to the recipe because that's how I like it.

text:
I came across this recipe in search of chocolate, and since it has been cool lately I thought I would give it a shot. I only made a single serving and used the microwave instead of the stove. I heated up the water for about 120 seconds (2 min.) and followed the directions from there. When I got to heating up the milk mixture I put it in the microwave for 45 sec., stirred, another 30 sec., stirred, and a final 15 sec. It was very creamy and I enjoyed it, but there was one thing that I didn't care for. I think that it was a little too sweet, but that doesn't interfere with the recipe. Ultimately, I will definitely make this again, and for others.

text:
Absolutely amazing.  Although pre-made mixes are far more convenient, they aren't anywhere near as creamy or chocolatey as this recipe turned out!  I wanted only two servings instead of four, so I cut the recipe in half; however, it only made enough cocoa for a mug and a half (I'd guess about 10 fl ounces, whereas I needed 16 to fill the mugs).  Next time I'll make it for three servings, just to ensure I have enough for two people.  Instead of half-and-half, I used heavy cream, because that's what I had on hand.  I also added a touch of cinnamon sugar on top for presentation and a little zing.  It was perfect on a chilly night!

text:
Very good. Much better than the last hot chocolate recipe I tried from this site that tasted like warm milk with a chocolate chip floating in it. (it was bad). This was very chocolaty and sweet and was much more like store bought hot cocoa. I didn't measure precisely, just eyeballed it, but I'm sure I got darn close to the actual measurements and it was not too sweet at all.  The only disappointment was that I cut the recipe in half because I was only serving myself and my husband and it didn't fill 2 mugs to the top, only about halfway on each. So if you are expecting to get 4 full mugs of hot cocoa from the 4 servings it lists, you better have small mugs. Next time I know to use the full recipe for two people.

text:
I made a big batch (4 x the ingredients)of this recipe for a gathering of friends.  It was a fun afternoon get-together of hot chocolate and a variety of homemade cookies.  Once the recipe was made, I transferred it to my slow cooker to keep warm.  I brought out some liquers and let everyone add their favourites to their cups.  Everyone liked it.  However, I found it a bit "powdery" in texture, and found some cocoa sludge at the bottom of the cooker after the party.  If making a big batch again, I would definitely use less cocoa powder and ensure that it was top-quality.  As per other reviews, I used less sugar (just under 2 cups).  Good idea!

text:
Wayyyy too sugary for me, but if you like those made ready to-go American grocery store cakes and cupcakes, don't tweak the recipe.

I reduced the amount of sugar from 2/3rd cups to just 1/3rd to level out the bitterness of the cocoa. The end result I'd say ended up tasting bitter/semisweet but was very good. I used whole milk and heavy cream.

Also, you can swap out the vanilla extract for pepper/spearmint for a more christmasy kick!

For me I like tasting the bitterness of chocolate; that's what makes something truly chocolate for me; no overbearing tooth pinching sweetness of sugar!

It's great if you decrease the amount of sugar (I used maple syrup which is a good substitute) by a LOT. Maple syrup and sugar are similar in sweetness, and even though I used only about 1/3 of a cup, it was a tiny bit too sweet, but still delicious.
I also increased the cacao powder to half (1/2) a cup, which made it more chocolatey, and therefore yummier.
The reason I didn't take a star off for the almost pure sugar recipe is that when you moderate the sweetener, it's perfect.
The cream on top is good too.

This is going in our permanent recipe book. Thank you!

text:
I am sitting here sipping on this wonderful recipe in bliss but also so ashamed of myself! Its been cold here the past couple of days, which lead to a hot chocolate craving. I actually went to the store and had the nerve to buy swiss miss instant hot chocolate even though I had Hershey's unsweetened cocoa powder in the cabinet. I bought the rich chocolate kind thinking that would make a difference. How wrong was I. NOTHING in the store will compare to this recipe. I reduced the sugar in this recipe as recommended by several other reviews.  Other than than I made no changes to the recipe itself. To enhance the flavor, I added a bit of unsweetened coffee creamer (If you use sweetened, I would reduce the sugar a bit more). I also topped it off with a hand full of marshmallows, drizzled a bit of hot fudge on top, and a dash of cinnamon. For those who wish to make an adult beverage out of their hot cocoa add a bit of rum, Kahlua, brandy, or your favorite liquor. Great recipe!!!

Great recipe!! I just tried it, and it's a hit at home! However, I did alter it a bit. I doubled the recipe in general, but I used 5 cups of raw whole milk (straight from the cow) and 2 cups of water, instead of using half-and-half (we didn't have any at the time). And since raw whole milk has the cream already in it/not removed, it's a perfect substitute, with the water to water it down, so it's not too thick. I also actually forgot to put in the vanilla extract, but my mom said it still tasted really good without it!
Success!

text:
Big hit at our Christmas Caroling party! I made 37 servings (to make it an even 2 gallons of milk) and found that I needed to double the water when mixing the cocoa and sugar.  Does not affect the end result but made it easier to mix. When heating up that much quantity you have to pay careful attention to the heat/flame to avoid scorching!  I had a bunch left over so I poured the remaining back into the plastic gallon milk container and took it to a friend's Christmas party where she heated it up and it was a hit there too.  Great with whip or marshmallows.
